The `baremetalds-devscripts-setup` pre-phase step failed to provision the OCP 4.21 baremetal cluster on Equinix Metal hardware. The `ocp_run` make target (`Makefile:83`) timed out after 1h13m because the cluster API endpoint at `192.168.111.5:6443` became unreachable — OVN networking (`ovnkube-node` DaemonSet) never stabilized, which cascaded to multiple control-plane operators (openshift-apiserver, oauth-apiserver, OLM, monitoring) remaining degraded. Since the pre-phase failed, **commatrix project tests never executed at all.** -
Full analysis
Based on all the evidence gathered, here is my analysis: --- **TL;DR:** Baremetal cluster installation failed (OVN stuck, API server unreachable); commatrix tests never ran. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: Baremetal cluster installation failure — OVN/API server never became healthy** (affects Tests:--- **TL;DR:** Baremetal OCP cluster install failed; API server unreachable — commatrix tests never ran. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: Baremetal cluster installation failure** (affects: all listed tests) - **Evidence:** ``` dial tcp 192.168.111.5:6443: connect: connection refused make: *** [Makefile:83: ocp_run] Error 1 + exit 2 Container test exited with code 2, reason Error (baremetalds-devscripts-setup, 1h13m54s) clusteroperator/network is not available (The network is starting up) because DaemonSet "/openshift-ovn-kubernetes/ovnkube-node" rollout is not making progress - last change 2026-07-21T13:36:32Z clusteroperator/openshift-apiserver is not available (APIServicesAvailable: PreconditionNotReady) because APIServerDeploymentDegraded: 2 of 3 requested instances are unavailable for apiserver.openshift-apiserver () clusteroperator/operator-lifecycle-manager-packageserver is not available (ClusterServiceVersion ... observed in phase Failed with reason: InstallCheckFailed, message: install timeout) ``` - **Root Cause:** The `baremetalds-devscripts-setup` pre-phase step failed to provision the OCP 4.21 baremetal cluster on Equinix Metal hardware. The `ocp_run` make target (`Makefile:83`) timed out after 1h13m because the cluster API endpoint at `192.168.111.5:6443` became unreachable — OVN networking (`ovnkube-node` DaemonSet) never stabilized, which cascaded to multiple control-plane operators (openshift-apiserver, oauth-apiserver, OLM, monitoring) remaining degraded. Since the pre-phase failed, **commatrix project tests never executed at all.** - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — this is a baremetal infra/nightly image provisioning failure, not traceable to a specific commatrix commit. - **Is it a flake?** Yes — baremetal cluster install failures due to OVN or bootstrap timeouts recur intermittently on Equinix Metal CI hardware. - **Suggested Fix:** Retry the job; if repeated, investigate the `4.21.0-0.nightly-2026-07-20-173555` release image for OVN or apiserver regressions, and check Equinix Metal node health for the `ofcir-50.cipool-ibmcloud.ofcir` host. - **Affected tests:** - `:OAuthServerServiceEndpointsEndpointAccessibleController_SyncError: APIServerDeploymentDegraded: 1 of 3 requested instances are unavailable for apiserver.openshift-oauth-apiserver ()` — CI framework cluster-health monitor, triggered by the degraded oauth-apiserver (cascade of install failure) - `:NodeController_MasterNodesReady: GuardControllerDegraded: [Missing operand on node master-1, Missing operand on node master-2]` — CI framework node-health monitor, triggered by missing operands on masters that never fully joined (cascade of install failure) --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause — baremetal cluster install failure; all test failures are cascades of the same event. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 4.21 nightly `4.21.0-0.nightly-2026-07-20-173555` — cluster install failed on Equinix Metal baremetal; OVN DaemonSet rollout stalled, multiple operators degraded. **Affected Images:** `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release:4.21.0-0.nightly-2026-07-20-173555` (190 component images imported; `ovnkube-node` and `oauth-apiserver` components suspect based on operator degradation patterns) **Overall Issue Class:** infra_other **Overall Severity:** MEDIUM

Commit `7d56343` (PR #400, "Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix", Feb 5 2026) stripped `DynamicRanges` from the generated commatrix. The test at `validation_test.go:159` calls `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges(missingEPSMat, commatrix.DynamicRanges)` — but `commatrix.DynamicRanges` is now empty, so the filter is a no-op. Crio binds to random ephemeral ports (32768–60999) on each node IP, which previously fell inside the dynamic range and were silently filtered. `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` at line 157 also does not handle `crio` (only `rpc.statd` and `dnsmasq`). Both filters now fail to exclude these ports, exposing the regression. -
Full analysis
Now I have enough to write the complete analysis. --- **TL;DR:** Crio ephemeral ports on 5 nodes fail the EndpointSlice check because dynamic-range filtering was removed. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: crio ephemeral ports have no EndpointSlice and are no longer filtered** (affects Test: `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports`) - **Evidence:** ``` [FAILED] the following ports are used but don't have an endpointslice: Ingress,TCP,44829,,crio,,,master,false Ingress,TCP,45195,,crio,,,master,false Ingress,TCP,45913,,crio,,,master,false Ingress,TCP,37363,,crio,,,worker,false Ingress,TCP,39509,,crio,,,worker,false Ingress,TCP,40519,,crio,,,worker,false ``` From `raw-ss-tcp`: `LISTEN 0 4096 192.168.111.20:44829 0.0.0.0:* users:(("crio",pid=4426,fd=12))` — confirmed as crio process on node IP, not a Kubernetes Service, so no EndpointSlice exists. - **Root Cause:** Commit `7d56343` (PR #400, "Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix", Feb 5 2026) stripped `DynamicRanges` from the generated commatrix. The test at `validation_test.go:159` calls `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges(missingEPSMat, commatrix.DynamicRanges)` — but `commatrix.DynamicRanges` is now empty, so the filter is a no-op. Crio binds to random ephemeral ports (32768–60999) on each node IP, which previously fell inside the dynamic range and were silently filtered. `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` at line 157 also does not handle `crio` (only `rpc.statd` and `dnsmasq`). Both filters now fail to exclude these ports, exposing the regression. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** `7d56343` / PR #400 — `https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/pull/400` - **Is it a flake?** No — crio always binds ephemeral ports on startup; the specific port numbers vary per run but the failure reproduces on every job. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `"crio"` to the `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` allowlist in `test/e2e/validation_test.go:221–239`, or restore ephemeral-range filtering specifically for the EndpointSlice check (separate from the matrix generation path). Alternatively, investigate whether crio's gRPC stream-server ports should carry a static `ComDetails` entry so they match an EndpointSlice. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` (`validation_test.go:141`) --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause group. The 7 stale matrix entries (`6388`, `8798` ×2, `9192`, `9443`, `UDP/68` ×2) only produce log warnings (`logrus.Warningf` at line 154) and do not contribute to the test failure; they represent documentation drift independent of the crio regression. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 5.0 (nightly 2026-06-22-235733) — failure is deterministic on this version due to missing dynamic-range filtering for crio ephemeral ports. **Affected Images:** `ci/telco-runner:latest` (test runner), `ocp-kni/test:dev-scripts` (cluster setup); no image pull errors — all images pulled successfully. **Overall Issue Class:** `test_regression` **Overall Severity:** HIGH

PR #400 / commit `7d56343` (`Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix`) deleted `getLinuxDynamicPrivateRange`, which previously appended the Linux kernel ephemeral port range (typically 32768–60999, read from `/proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_local_port_range`) to `commatrix.DynamicRanges`. CRI-O's streaming server binds to an ephemeral port on the node's external IP (38919 here, always in the Linux ephemeral range). Before PR #400, `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` would suppress it; now `DynamicRanges` only contains the Kubernetes NodePort range (~30000–32767), leaving 38919 unfiltered. The test fails at `validation_test.go:161`.
Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** CRI-O's ephemeral port (38919) now exposed after Linux dynamic-range filter removal in PR #400. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: CRI-O ephemeral port no longer suppressed by dynamic-range filter** (affects Tests: `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports`) - **Evidence:** ``` [FAILED] the following ports are used but don't have an endpointslice: Ingress,TCP,38919,,crio,,,master,false ``` From `raw-ss-tcp`: `LISTEN 0 4096 10.0.71.48:38919 0.0.0.0:* users:(("crio",pid=4187,fd=11))` The failing test is at `validation_test.go:161` — after calling `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (which skips `rpc.statd`, `dnsmasq`, `dig` but **not** `crio`) and `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges(missingEPSMat, commatrix.DynamicRanges)`, port 38919 survives both filters and causes the `Fail(...)` call. - **Root Cause:** PR #400 / commit `7d56343` (`Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix`) deleted `getLinuxDynamicPrivateRange`, which previously appended the Linux kernel ephemeral port range (typically 32768–60999, read from `/proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_local_port_range`) to `commatrix.DynamicRanges`. CRI-O's streaming server binds to an ephemeral port on the node's external IP (38919 here, always in the Linux ephemeral range). Before PR #400, `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` would suppress it; now `DynamicRanges` only contains the Kubernetes NodePort range (~30000–32767), leaving 38919 unfiltered. The test fails at `validation_test.go:161`. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** `7d56343` merged via PR #400 (`https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/pull/400`), present on both `main` and `release-5.0` branches. - **Is it a flake?** No — crio always allocates an ephemeral port outside 30000–32767 on the node IP; this will fail consistently after PR #400 on every single-node run. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `crio` to the `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` function in `validation_test.go` (alongside `rpc.statd`), since CRI-O's streaming server port is an internal ephemeral port not intended to be documented in the communication matrix. Alternatively, reintroduce a targeted ephemeral-range filter for services known to use random ports. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` (`validation_test.go:161`) --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause — one PR removed the Linux ephemeral-range guard, exposing crio's random port. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 5.0 (SNO, AWS, OVN): fails consistently after PR #400 merged Feb 5 2026. **Affected Images:** `quay.io/openshift-release-dev/ocp-v5.0-art-dev` (test container), commatrix test binary built from `release-5.0` branch. **Overall Issue Class:** `matrix_mismatch` **Overall Severity:** MEDIUM

Then `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` (line 159) uses `commatrix.DynamicRanges`, but PR #400 (commit `7d56343`, "Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix") removed the 32768-60999 ephemeral range from the generated matrix, leaving only the NodePort range 30000-32767 (`KubeletNodePortDefaultDynamicRange`, `static-custom-entries.go:365`). crio's ephemeral ports fall above 32767, so they pass through both filters and cause the assertion failure. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** PR #400 / commit `7d56343` — "Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix" (merged on `main`; confirmed on `release-5.0` by the fact that the ephemeral-range filter is absent in the failing test run, which clones from `release-5.0`) - **Is it a flake?** No — crio consistently opens ephemeral TCP ports on every node (one per master, one per worker per node for gRPC/container management); this will fail on every run until `crio` is added to the known-services skip list. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `crio` to the skip list in `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` in `test/e2e/validation_test.go:226-228`, analogous to the existing `rpc.statd` skip. Alternatively, re-add the Linux ephemeral range (32768-60999) to the test-side dynamic range filter without adding it back to the generated matrix output. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause group. The 7 stale matrix entries (TCP/6388 metal3-httpd, TCP/8798 machine-config-daemon ×2, TCP/9192 machine-approver, TCP/9443 cloud-controller-manager, UDP/68 NetworkManager ×2) generate warnings only in the first test (`generated communication matrix should be equal to documented communication matrix`) which **passed** — they are a documentation debt but not the cause of the job failure. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 5.0 nightly (5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-29-195240) — failing consistently due to the absent crio filter. **Affected Images:** No image pull failures; all images resolved successfully. CRI-O (the container runtime, PID 2709) opens a randomly-assigned ephemeral port (36239, in the Linux range 32768–60999) that has no Kubernetes EndpointSlice. `validation_test.go:159` calls `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges(missingEPSMat, commatrix.DynamicRanges)`, but `commatrix.DynamicRanges` is populated by `GetDynamicRanges()` (`pkg/dynamic-ranges/dynamic-ranges.go`) which returns only the Kubernetes NodePort range (30000–32767). Port 36239 > 32767, so it is not filtered. Prior to PR #400 (`7d56343`), the Linux ephemeral range was included in `DynamicRanges` and this port would have been filtered; that PR removed it to prevent the firewall matrix from leaving all ephemeral ports open, but also broke the EPS validation filter. -
Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** CRI-O's ephemeral port (36239) is open but has no EndpointSlice and is not filtered after PR #400 removed Linux dynamic ranges. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: CRI-O ephemeral port not filtered by EPS validation test** (affects Tests: `[It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports`) - **Evidence:** ``` [FAIL] Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports /tmp/secret/commatrix/test/e2e/validation_test.go:161 ``` `Port 36239: LISTEN 0 4096 10.0.1.66:36239 0.0.0.0:* users:(("crio",pid=2709,fd=12))` `matrix-diff-ss: - Ingress,TCP,36239,,crio,,,master,false` - **Root Cause:** CRI-O (the container runtime, PID 2709) opens a randomly-assigned ephemeral port (36239, in the Linux range 32768–60999) that has no Kubernetes EndpointSlice. `validation_test.go:159` calls `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges(missingEPSMat, commatrix.DynamicRanges)`, but `commatrix.DynamicRanges` is populated by `GetDynamicRanges()` (`pkg/dynamic-ranges/dynamic-ranges.go`) which returns only the Kubernetes NodePort range (30000–32767). Port 36239 > 32767, so it is not filtered. Prior to PR #400 (`7d56343`), the Linux ephemeral range was included in `DynamicRanges` and this port would have been filtered; that PR removed it to prevent the firewall matrix from leaving all ephemeral ports open, but also broke the EPS validation filter. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** `1fec55d` Merge pull request #400 from shirmoran/remove-linux-dynamic-range (`7d56343` "Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix") - **Is it a flake?** No — CRI-O consistently opens an ephemeral port above 32767 on every cluster, so this failure will recur on every run until fixed. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `"crio"` to the `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` allowlist in `test/e2e/validation_test.go` (alongside the existing `rpc.statd` filter), since CRI-O is a host-level process that opens random ephemeral ports with no EndpointSlice by design. Alternatively, add a separate Linux ephemeral range filter (32768–60999) to the EPS validation check without putting it back into the generated firewall matrix. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause. The 7 stale matrix entries (TCP 80, 443, 8798, 9099, 9192, 9443, 10258 — documented or EPS-generated but not actually open on the SNO node) generate only `logrus.Warning` calls (lines 108–110 and 153–155 of `validation_test.go`) and do not fail any test. They indicate the `docs/stable/raw/aws-sno.csv` documented matrix is drifting from actual OCP 4.23 SNO port usage but are not the direct failure cause. **Per-Version Notes:** - OCP 4.23 (evidence): CRI-O ephemeral port 36239 fails the EPS validation; 7 stale matrix entries logged as warnings. - OCP 5.0 (no evidence file): Same root cause expected — identical `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` logic and `GetDynamicRanges` returning only NodePort range; CRI-O ephemeral port behavior unchanged. **Affected Images:** `ci/telco-runner:latest` (test runner); OCP release `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release:4.23.0-0.nightly-2026-06-24-155843` **Overall Issue Class:** `matrix_mismatch` **Overall Severity:** HIGH

The `telco5g-sno-setup` step ran an Ansible playbook (`ocp-install.yml`) to provision an OCP 4.21 nightly SNO cluster on bare metal node `cnfdu14.upstreamci.bos2.lab`. After ~2.5 hours, the cluster API server at `192.168.17.121:6443` was still completely unreachable ("no route to host"), meaning the install never completed or the node never came up. The "RETRYING: Run oc command to check if cluster is ready" failures are Ansible retry loop iterations in `ocp-install.yml` (lines 38/46/58) waiting for the API — not commatrix test assertions. The commatrix project tests were never reached. -
Full analysis

The Ansible `ocp-install.yml` playbook on the `telco5g-cluster-setup` step polled for an install-finished marker file on bare-metal host `cnfdu21`. The OCP 4.21 installer never completed within the allowed window, so the loop exhausted all 150 retries and exited with code 2 after 2h43m. CRI-O binds ephemeral TCP ports (32768–60999 range) on both master and worker nodes at runtime; these have no Kubernetes EndpointSlice. Two filters protect against spurious failures: `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (excludes `rpc.statd`, `dnsmasq`, `dig` — but **not** `crio`) and `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` (excludes ports within `commatrix.DynamicRanges` — but commit `7d56343` intentionally removed the Linux ephemeral range from the generated commatrix). Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** CRI-O ephemeral TCP ports lack EndpointSlice entries and are not filtered, causing the matrix-vs-ss validation test to fail. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: CRI-O ephemeral TCP ports pass through all filters unblocked** (affects Test: `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` — `test/e2e/validation_test.go:161`) - **Evidence:** ``` [FAILED] the following ports are used but don't have an endpointslice: Ingress,TCP,40803,,crio,,,master,false Ingress,TCP,40999,,crio,,,master,false Ingress,TCP,44465,,crio,,,master,false Ingress,TCP,39127,,crio,,,worker,false Ingress,TCP,41873,,crio,,,worker,false Ingress,TCP,44687,,crio,,,worker,false ``` From `build-log.txt:180-187` and `matrix-diff-ss` (all six `-` prefixed crio entries). - **Root Cause:** CRI-O binds ephemeral TCP ports (32768–60999 range) on both master and worker nodes at runtime; these have no Kubernetes EndpointSlice. Two filters protect against spurious failures: `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (excludes `rpc.statd`, `dnsmasq`, `dig` — but **not** `crio`) and `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` (excludes ports within `commatrix.DynamicRanges` — but commit `7d56343` intentionally removed the Linux ephemeral range from the generated commatrix). In `validation_test.go:157-161`, `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` only skips `rpc.statd`/`dnsmasq`; `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` (line 159) consults `commatrix.DynamicRanges`, which after commit `7d56343` ("Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix", PR #400) no longer includes the 32768-60999 ephemeral range — only the NodePort range 30000-32767. TCP 36039 therefore survives both filters and triggers `Fail()` at line 161. The ovnkube nodeport ports (30146/30767/32633) and rpc.statd ports are correctly filtered, leaving only TCP 36039 as the trigger. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** `7d56343` / PR #400 (`1fec55d Merge pull request #400 from shirmoran/remove-linux-dynamic-range`) — removed the Linux ephemeral range from the generated commatrix and thus from `DynamicRanges`. - **Is it a flake?** No — this is a regression; the specific ephemeral port number varies per boot but the root cause (missing ephemeral range from DynamicRanges) is deterministic and will reproduce on every run. - **Suggested Fix:** Either re-add crio (and similar host-level ephemeral services) to the `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` allowlist in `validation_test.go`, or re-introduce the Linux ephemeral range (32768-60999) as a filtered dynamic range separate from the generated commatrix documentation. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` (validation_test.go:161) - **Group 2: Stale entries in documented matrix for OCP 4.23 SNO (warnings, not direct failure)** - **Evidence:** ``` doc-diff-commatrix: - Ingress,TCP,80,openshift-ingress,router-default,... - Ingress,TCP,443,openshift-ingress,router-default,... - Ingress,TCP,8798,openshift-machine-config-operator,... - Ingress,TCP,9192,openshift-cluster-machine-approver,... matrix-diff-ss: + Ingress,TCP,9443,openshift-cloud-controller-manager-operator,... + Ingress,TCP,10258,openshift-cloud-controller-manager,... ``` - **Root Cause:** `docs/stable/raw/aws-sno.csv` contains 6 ports no longer active on OCP 4.23 SNO: TCP 80/443 (router-default ingress pods not exposing EndpointSlices in SNO topology), TCP 8798 (MCD now internal on 127.0.0.1:8797), TCP 9192 (machine-approver kube-rbac-proxy port changed), TCP 9443/10258 (cloud-controller-manager-operator ports reorganized). These cause only `logrus.Warningf` calls (lines 108-110 and 154-155) and do NOT directly trigger the test failure, but the documented CSV needs updating for 4.23. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown (OCP 4.23 infrastructure-side changes removed/moved these services). - **Is it a flake?** No — these services are consistently absent on this 4.23 SNO cluster. - **Suggested Fix:** Update `docs/stable/raw/aws-sno.csv` to remove TCP 80, 443, 8798, 9192 and reconcile 9443/10258 entries to reflect the 4.23 SNO port layout. - **Affected tests:** "generated communication matrix should be equal to documented communication matrix" (warnings only, test passed). --- **Relation Between Groups:** Groups 1 and 2 are independent — Group 1 is caused by a code regression in commatrix (PR #400 removed ephemeral range filtering), while Group 2 reflects OCP 4.23 infrastructure-side port changes that haven't been reflected in the documented matrix CSV. Group 2 doesn't cause test failure; Group 1 does. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 4.23 (SNO/AWS): Both issues present; Group 1 is the direct failure cause. **Affected Images:** `quay.io/openshift-release-dev/ocp-v4.0-art-dev@sha256:c1cb03332d3a5e641eac1ae9732b0924a94a50d3b95866d112bb7c5a12cf0d51` (debug pod), `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release:4.23.0-0.nightly-2026-06-25-142049` **Overall Issue Class:** matrix_mismatch **Overall Severity:** MEDIUM

The BeforeEach at `validation_test.go:47–54` runs `oc commatrix generate --host-open-ports`, which in `pkg/listening-sockets/listening-sockets.go:119` calls `RunCommandOnPod(debugPod, []string{"/bin/sh", "-c", "ss -anpltH"})` — a `kubectl exec`-style call routed through the kubelet streaming API on port 10250. The API server got `connection refused` when dialing the node's kubelet port 10250, meaning kubelet's exec endpoint was unreachable on that node. The most likely cause on a reused bare-metal cluster is residual nftables rules from a prior periodic CI run that did not include port 10250 in the allow list; the generated `communication-matrix-worker.nft` for this run does include port 10250, but that rule had not yet been applied when the test started. -

--- **TL;DR:** Both Validation tests failed because `oc commatrix generate --host-open-ports` could not reach the kubelet API (port 10250 `connection refused`) on a node. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: Kubelet exec API (port 10250) connection refused** (affects both Validation tests) - **Evidence:** ``` error: failed to generate matrix: failed to generate SS matrix: error while generating the listening check matrix and ss raws: remote command [/bin/sh -c ss -anpltH] error [error dialing backend: dial tcp XXXXXXXXXXXX43:10250: connect: connection refused]. output [] ``` Both Validation BeforeEach failures at `validation_test.go:48` share this identical error (15:05:15 and 15:06:19 respectively). - **Root Cause:** The BeforeEach at `validation_test.go:47–54` runs `oc commatrix generate --host-open-ports`, which in `pkg/listening-sockets/listening-sockets.go:119` calls `RunCommandOnPod(debugPod, []string{"/bin/sh", "-c", "ss -anpltH"})` — a `kubectl exec`-style call routed through the kubelet streaming API on port 10250. The API server got `connection refused` when dialing the node's kubelet port 10250, meaning kubelet's exec endpoint was unreachable on that node. The most likely cause on a reused bare-metal cluster is residual nftables rules from a prior periodic CI run that did not include port 10250 in the allow list; the generated `communication-matrix-worker.nft` for this run does include port 10250, but that rule had not yet been applied when the test started. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — no recent code change caused this; it's a cluster-state issue. The nftables test (which passed) runs later and generates rules that do allow port 10250. - **Is it a flake?** Yes — periodic bare-metal CI jobs reuse the same cluster; if a previous run's MCO-applied nftables rules blocked kubelet port 10250, subsequent runs fail until the cluster is reset or the rules are updated. - **Suggested Fix:** Add a pre-test cleanup step in the CI job to flush or verify residual nftables rules (especially the `openshift_filter` chain) before the Validation test suite runs. Alternatively, add a retry or wait loop in `GenerateSS` to tolerate transient kubelet exec failures. - **Affected tests:** - `Validation [BeforeEach] generated communication matrix should be equal to documented communication matrix` (`validation_test.go:62`) - `Validation [BeforeEach] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` (`validation_test.go:138`) --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause — both Validation tests share the same BeforeEach block (`validation_test.go:41–64`) and both failed on the identical error. The Nftables test (which passed) uses `oc commatrix generate --format nft` (no `--host-open-ports`) and never calls the kubelet exec API, confirming the problem is isolated to the kubelet streaming path. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 4.21 nightly `4.21.0-0.nightly-2026-06-25-091937` — cluster setup succeeded, only the kubelet exec API path was broken at test time. **Affected Images:** `ci/telco-runner:latest` (test runner), `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release:4.21.0-0.nightly-2026-06-25-091937` **Overall Issue Class:** infra_other **Overall Severity:** MEDIUM

The crio container runtime is listening on ephemeral TCP port 34279 bound to the specific node IP `10.0.91.164` (not `0.0.0.0`). This port has no Kubernetes EndpointSlice (it is a host-level process, not a Kubernetes Service), and it is not present in the documented communication matrix. The test at `validation_test.go:161` strictly requires every detected open port to have a backing EndpointSlice, so crio's untracked socket causes a hard FAIL. The port number (within Linux ephemeral range 32768–60999) is randomly assigned by the OS and will differ on each reboot or crio restart. -
Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** OCP 5.0 SNO port landscape diverged from commatrix: 1 crio ephemeral port causes hard fail, 4 stale matrix entries, 2 cloud-controller ports missing EndpointSlice. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: crio ephemeral port open with no EndpointSlice** (affects Tests: `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports`) - **Evidence:** ``` [FAILED] the following ports are used but don't have an endpointslice: Ingress,TCP,34279,,crio,,,master,false ``` ``` Port 34279: LISTEN 0 4096 10.0.91.164:34279 0.0.0.0:* users:(("crio",pid=4133,fd=12)) ``` - **Root Cause:** The crio container runtime is listening on ephemeral TCP port 34279 bound to the specific node IP `10.0.91.164` (not `0.0.0.0`). This port has no Kubernetes EndpointSlice (it is a host-level process, not a Kubernetes Service), and it is not present in the documented communication matrix. The test at `validation_test.go:161` strictly requires every detected open port to have a backing EndpointSlice, so crio's untracked socket causes a hard FAIL. The port number (within Linux ephemeral range 32768–60999) is randomly assigned by the OS and will differ on each reboot or crio restart. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — this appears to be a new crio behavior in OCP 5.0 nightly `5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-24-153432`; no specific PR identified. - **Is it a flake?** Potentially yes — the ephemeral port number changes every reboot, meaning the port may not always be visible at test-capture time, but the underlying condition (crio listening on a node-IP-bound port with no EndpointSlice) is structural. - **Suggested Fix:** Either add a static commatrix entry for crio's metrics/stream socket on the node IP (with `Optional:true`), or update the test's EndpointSlice validation to exclude ports belonging to known host-level processes (crio, rpcbind, rpc.statd) that cannot have EndpointSlices by design. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` (`validation_test.go:161`) - **Group 2: Stale documented-matrix entries — services not running on OCP 5.0 SNO AWS** (affects: warning emitted, contributes to "6 in matrix but not in use" count) - **Evidence:** ``` level=warning msg="the following ports are documented but are not used: Ingress,TCP,80,openshift-ingress,router-default,... Ingress,TCP,443,openshift-ingress,router-default,... Ingress,TCP,8798,openshift-machine-config-operator,machine-config-daemon,... Ingress,TCP,9192,openshift-cluster-machine-approver,machine-approver,..." ``` ``` # matrix-diff-summary.txt: Ports in matrix but not in use on node: Ingress,TCP,80 / 443 / 8798 / 9192 / 9443 / 10258 ``` - **Root Cause:** Four ports (TCP 80, 443, 8798, 9192) exist in the documented OCP 5.0 commatrix but are not open on the single-node AWS cluster. Router ports 80/443 may not be active on SNO, `machine-config-daemon` port 8798 (internal health) moved or was removed, and the `machine-approver` kube-rbac-proxy port 9192 is absent. These are stale entries in `doc/aws-sno` commatrix CSV that were never updated for OCP 5.0 / SNO topology changes. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — likely reflects incremental OCP 5.0 component changes that were never reconciled back into the commatrix docs. - **Is it a flake?** No — these ports are consistently absent on SNO; this is a documentation gap. - **Suggested Fix:** Remove TCP 80, 443, 8798, 9192 from the documented AWS SNO commatrix, or mark them `Optional:true` with an SNO-exception note. - **Affected tests:** Logged as warnings; does not directly fail a test but inflates the "6 in matrix but not in use" count reported in the job reason. - **Group 3: Cloud-controller-manager ports open but missing EndpointSlice** (affects: "open but missing endpointslice" count) - **Evidence:** ``` # matrix-diff-summary.txt: Ports open but missing EndpointSlice: Ingress,TCP,9443,openshift-cloud-controller-manager-operator,...cluster-cloud-controller-manager... Ingress,TCP,10258,openshift-cloud-controller-manager,aws-cloud-controller-manager,... ``` ``` level=warning msg="the following ports are not used: Ingress,TCP,9443,... Ingress,TCP,10258,...\n" ``` - **Root Cause:** TCP 9443 (`cloud-controller-manager-operator`) and TCP 10258 (`aws-cloud-controller-manager`) are actively listening on the node but have no corresponding EndpointSlice. These are OCP platform services (not commatrix code). In OCP 5.0 the cloud-controller-manager moved from `openshift-cloud-controller-manager-operator` delivering via a Service+EndpointSlice to a static pod or host-network deployment that skips Service object creation, so no EndpointSlice is generated. The documented matrix still lists them as EndpointSlice-backed entries. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — likely an upstream OCP 5.0 cloud-controller-manager architecture change; see `openshift-cloud-controller-manager-operator` release notes for OCP 5.0. - **Is it a flake?** No — this is a structural gap: the cloud-controller services consistently lack EndpointSlice in OCP 5.0 SNO. - **Suggested Fix:** File a Jira against `openshift-cloud-controller-manager-operator` to ensure an EndpointSlice is created for ports 9443/10258, or update the commatrix static-entries to mark these as host-process ports not requiring EndpointSlice validation. - **Affected tests:** Does not fail the test directly (treated as warning), but contributes to the "open but missing endpointslice" count in the job failure reason. --- **Relation Between Groups:** All three groups share the same upstream cause: the OCP 5.0 SNO platform port landscape has drifted from the commatrix documentation and assumptions. Group 1 is the only hard test failure; Groups 2 and 3 are unresolved data inconsistencies that inflate the mismatch counts. There is no image pull failure or CI infrastructure failure — the cluster deployed successfully and 3 of 4 test specs passed. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 5.0 (`5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-24-153432`, SNO/AWS/OVN) — commatrix docs need updating for SNO topology; cloud-controller-manager EndpointSlice gap is specific to 5.0 architecture. **Affected Images:** `quay.io/openshift-release-dev/ocp-v5.0-art-dev@sha256:c439d20d39a77f862424a2f194f44b9789091e7523ae82c514ee0b0205b2d8ae` (test runner); OCP release `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release-5:5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-24-153432` **Overall Issue Class:** matrix_mismatch **Overall Severity:** MEDIUM — the cluster and workloads are healthy; the failure reflects documentation/EndpointSlice gaps, not a broken OCP component. The gap likely predates this run or was introduced when the `crio` exclusion was omitted from `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices`. - **Is it a flake?** Partially — the specific port numbers change on every reboot/restart (ephemeral assignment), but crio consistently opens such sockets, so this likely reproduces on every run until the filter is fixed. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `crio` to the `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` exclusion list in `validation_test.go:221`, or expand `commatrix.DynamicRanges` to include the full Linux ephemeral port range (32768–60999) for TCP on both master and worker pools. Either approach will prevent non-deterministic crio gRPC/internal sockets from failing the EndpointSlice check. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` - **Group 2: Stale ports in documented matrix (warnings only — not causing failure)** - **Evidence:** ``` - Ingress,TCP,8798,openshift-machine-config-operator,machine-config-daemon,...,master,false - Ingress,TCP,9192,openshift-cluster-machine-approver,machine-approver,...,master,false - Ingress,TCP,8798,...,worker,false - Ingress,TCP,9443,openshift-cloud-controller-manager-operator,...,master,false - Ingress,UDP,68,,NetworkManager,,,master,false - Ingress,UDP,68,,NetworkManager,,,worker,false ``` Code: `logrus.Warningf("the following ports are not used: \n %s", notUsedEPSMat)` — this is a warning, not a `Fail()`. - **Root Cause:** Six entries in the documented matrix (`docs/stable/raw/*.csv`) are no longer active on OCP 4.23: `machine-config-daemon` dropped TCP/8798, `machine-approver` dropped TCP/9192, `cloud-controller-manager-operator` moved away from TCP/9443, and `NetworkManager` UDP/68 (DHCP) is not persistently listening. These do not cause a test failure today but indicate the documented matrix is out of date for 4.23. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — likely a 4.23 platform change removed these ports. - **Is it a flake?** No — these ports are consistently absent. - **Suggested Fix:** Remove the 6 stale entries from the documented matrix CSV files; add TCP/9443 for `cloud-controller-manager-operator` if it is now in use (it appears with `+` in `matrix-diff-ss`). - **Affected tests:** None currently (warnings only), but will need updating to keep matrix accurate. --- **Relation Between Groups:** The two groups are independent. Now I have everything I need to write the complete analysis. --- ### Test 1: `[Validation] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` - **Duration:** 20.809 seconds (within the 448.895s overall suite run) - **Error:** `the following ports are used but don't have an endpointslice: Ingress,TCP,44463,,crio,,,master,false` — triggered at `test/e2e/validation_test.go:161` - **Root Cause:** Port TCP 44463 is bound by the CRI-O container runtime process (pid=2677) as an ephemeral host-level socket (`LISTEN 0 4096 10.0.82.179:44463 0.0.0.0:*`). Because it is a host process, no Kubernetes EndpointSlice exists for it. Prior to PR #400, the generated `commatrix.DynamicRanges` included the Linux ephemeral private port range (32768–60999), and the call to `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` at `validation_test.go:159` would have silently discarded port 44463 (which falls in that range). PR #400 removed `getLinuxDynamicPrivateRange` from `pkg/dynamic-ranges/dynamic-ranges.go` and deleted `types.LinuxDynamicPrivateDefaultDynamicRange`, leaving only the Kubernetes NodePort range (30000–32767) as a dynamic filter. Port 44463 is outside that range, and `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (`validation_test.go:221–239`) only exempts `rpc.statd`, `dnsmasq`, and `dig` — not `crio` — so the port survives all filtering and causes the `Fail` at line 161. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** [PR #400 — "Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix"](https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/pull/400) — merged 2026-04-28, commit `7d56343e0d6e32f2fcc9b639ada47bb83cc57740`. The specific change that broke the test was the deletion of `LinuxDynamicPrivateDefaultDynamicRange` from `pkg/types/static-custom-entries.go` and the removal of `getLinuxDynamicPrivateRange` from `pkg/dynamic-ranges/dynamic-ranges.go`, which together stripped the 32768–60999 dynamic-range filter from the validation path. - **Source File:** https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/blob/main/test/e2e/validation_test.go#L161 - **Is it a flake?** Likely yes for the specific port number, but structurally a deterministic regression. Port 44463 is an ephemeral OS-assigned port; on any given run the exact port number from CRI-O will differ, but CRI-O consistently opens an ephemeral host-level socket (for internal streaming/gRPC) that lands in the 32768–60999 range. Before PR #400, every such port was silently filtered. After PR #400, every run where CRI-O's ephemeral port lands outside 30000–32767 (i.e. practically every run) will fail. The failure mode is therefore structurally consistent, even if the exact port number varies per run. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `crio` (and potentially any other known container-runtime host processes) to the `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` function in `test/e2e/validation_test.go`, following the same pattern already used for `rpc.statd` (line 226–229). CRI-O is a host-level daemon that will never have an EndpointSlice; treating it exactly like `rpc.statd` is the correct semantic. A broader but also valid fix is to re-introduce the Linux ephemeral range as a separate, test-only filter (not in the firewall matrix), so any ephemeral host process is automatically excluded from the EPS validation without re-opening the firewall concern that motivated PR #400. --- **Relation Between Failures:** There is only one failed test. Let me write the full analysis. --- ### Test 1: `network-flow-matrix-tests` - **Duration:** 72s - **Error:** Cluster API unreachable → `get_cluster_version()` returns `.` → `git checkout release-.` fails with pathspec error - **Evidence:** ``` Unable to connect to the server: dial tcp 10.1.104.200:64422: i/o timeout Go version: go version go1.22.4 linux/amd64 Cloning into '/tmp/secret/commatrix'... /tmp/secret/commatrix / error: pathspec 'release-.' did not match any file(s) known to git ``` - **Root Cause:** The SNO cluster API at `10.1.104.200:64422` was unreachable when the test step started. The test script's `get_cluster_version()` function runs `oc version | grep "Server Version:"` — but since the cluster is unreachable, `oc version` emits only a connection error to stderr and the grep matches nothing, leaving `version=""`. The function then computes `echo "$major.$minor"` where both are empty, returning `.`. This makes `cluster_version="."` and `testing_branch="release-."`, causing `git checkout release-.` to fail. The git error is a cascade; the first domino is the unreachable cluster API. Source: `get_cluster_version()` in the `network-flow-matrix-tests` step script at [steps.ci.openshift.org/reference/network-flow-matrix-tests](https://steps.ci.openshift.org/reference/network-flow-matrix-tests). - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — this is an infra failure, not a code regression. - **Source File:** [steps.ci.openshift.org/reference/network-flow-matrix-tests](https://steps.ci.openshift.org/reference/network-flow-matrix-tests) (openshift/release step registry) - **Is it a flake?** Yes — transient infrastructure network failure; the test script logic itself is also fragile when the cluster is unreachable. - **Suggested Fix:** Retry the job. Additionally, `get_cluster_version()` should check whether `oc version` succeeded (or use `oc version --client` to avoid server calls for version detection) and exit with a clear error rather than silently producing a malformed branch name. --- ### Test 2: `gather-must-gather` - **Duration:** 548s (9m8s) - **Error:** Cluster API unreachable — all `oc adm must-gather` calls time out - **Evidence:** ``` E0622 14:25:51.490744 51 memcache.go:265] "Unhandled Error" err="couldn't get current server API group list: Get \"https://10.1.104.200:64422/api?timeout=32s\": dial tcp 10.1.104.200:64422: i/o timeout" error completing cluster type inspection: error running backup collection: Get "https://10.1.104.200:64422/api?timeout=32s": dial tcp 10.1.104.200:64422: i/o timeout error: creating temp namespace: Post "https://10.1.104.200:64422/api/v1/namespaces": dial tcp 10.1.104.200:64422: i/o timeout ``` - **Root Cause:** Same as Test 1 — the SNO cluster API at `10.1.104.200:64422` is completely unresponsive. `must-gather` repeatedly retries with 32s timeouts for 9 minutes before giving up.
